## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science where constitutive laws describe how stress depends on strain and temperature, typically involving strain hardening and thermal softening effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at small strains)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening without temperature)
- Hollomon with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (combined hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (hardening with nonlinear thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating exponential hardening)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Combined Ludwik-thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (Ludwik with exponential thermal softening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Swift with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power-law with Arrhenius softening)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) * (c2 + c3 * T + c4 * T**2) (polynomial constitutive model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening behavior â†’ Power-law form epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 (work hardening exponent typically between 0.1 and 0.5)
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus â†’ Multiplicative factor (c0 - c1*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to the strain-dependent term
- Saturating flow stress â†’ Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation
- Yield stress offset â†’ Additive constant (c0 + f(epsilon)) separating initial yield from hardening contribution
- Thermally activated deformation â†’ Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) reflecting thermal activation of dislocation motion
- Shifted strain origin â†’ (epsilon + c)**n form (Swift model) accounting for pre-strain or elastic-plastic transition
- Separable temperature-strain coupling â†’ sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) where stress factorizes into independent strain and temperature functions
- Homologous temperature scaling â†’ Temperature appears as (T/c0) raised to a power, reflecting normalized thermal effects relative to melting point

**Candidate 2:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2 + c_2\exp(Tc_3 + c_4/\sqrt{\epsilon}) + c_5\epsilon^{c_6}\exp(c_7\epsilon^{c_8})$
- $T^{1/3}$ instead of $T$, $\epsilon^2$ term, exp with $1/\sqrt{\epsilon}$. Cannot match. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** $T^{c_0}c_1\log(c_2\epsilon+1) + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5\sin(c_6\log(Tc_7\epsilon+1)+c_8)$
- $\log$ and $\sin$ basis functions, no Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** $c_0\exp(c_1\epsilon)/T^{0.25} + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\exp(c_5\epsilon) + c_6 + c_7\exp(Tc_8 + c_9/\epsilon)$
- Has $T^{-0.25}$, exp terms not quadratic in T. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon + c_2\epsilon^{c_3}\exp(c_4/T) + c_5 + c_6\exp(Tc_7 + c_8\epsilon^{c_9})$
- $T^{1/3}$ not $T$, $\exp(c/T)$ not Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** $c_0 + c_1\epsilon + c_2\exp(Tc_3 + c_4\epsilon^{c_5}) + c_6\epsilon\exp(c_7/T) + c_8\epsilon^2\exp(c_9/T)$
- Has $\exp(c/T)$ terms, not Gaussian in T. The exp term $\exp(Tc_3 + c_4\epsilon^{c_5})$ is linear in T in exponent, not quadratic. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** $Tc_0 + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + c_3 + c_4\exp(c_5\epsilon) + c_6\exp(Tc_7 + c_8\epsilon^{c_9})$
- Not linear in $\epsilon$. Terms like $Tc_0$ have no $\epsilon$. Setting $c_0=0, c_1=0, c_3=0$ kills the T-linear part. Can't work. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** $Tc_0 + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + Tc_3\epsilon\exp(Tc_4) + c_5 + c_6\exp(c_7\epsilon) + c_8\exp(Tc_9\epsilon)$
- $Tc_3\epsilon\exp(Tc_4)$ - this is $\epsilon T\exp(c_4 T)$, not matching Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** Similar structure to 7, not linear in $\epsilon$. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** $c_0\exp(c_1\epsilon)/T^{0.25} + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3\epsilon^2 + c_4 + c_5\epsilon^{c_6} + c_7\exp(Tc_8 + c_9/\epsilon)$
- Has $T\epsilon$ which is good, but $T\epsilon^2$, $T^{-0.25}$, $\exp(T c_8 + c_9/\epsilon)$ (linear in T in exponent). No Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 11:** $Tc_0 + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + c_3 + c_4\exp(c_5\epsilon) + c_6\exp(Tc_7\epsilon) + c_8\epsilon\exp(Tc_9)$
- Last term: $c_8\epsilon\exp(c_9 T)$ - exponential in T, not Gaussian. Not linear in $\epsilon$ overall. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 12:** $c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2\exp(c_2/T) + c_3(c_4+\epsilon)^5\exp(c_5/T) + c_6 + c_7\exp(c_8\epsilon^{c_9})$
- $(c_4+\epsilon)^5$ creates high-order $\epsilon$ terms. $\exp(c/T)$ not Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 13:** $Tc_0 + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + c_3 + c_4\exp(c_5\epsilon) + c_6\exp(Tc_7\epsilon) + c_8\epsilon^2\exp(Tc_9)$
- Not linear in $\epsilon$. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 14:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2 + c_2\epsilon^{c_3}(Tc_4)^{c_5} + c_6\exp(Tc_7 + c_8/\sqrt{\epsilon}) + c_9\epsilon^{c_3}\exp(Tc_7)$

Wait, let me re-read: $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2 + c_2\exp(Tc_3 + c_4\epsilon^{c_5}) + c_6\exp(Tc_7) + c_8\epsilon^{c_9}\exp(Tc_7)$

- $T^{1/3}$ not $T$. Exp terms linear in T. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 15:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2 + c_2\exp(Tc_3 + c_4\epsilon^{c_5}) + c_6 + c_7\epsilon^{c_8}\exp(Tc_9)$
- $T^{1/3}$ not $T$. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 16:** $c_0 + c_1\epsilon^{c_2} + c_3\exp(Tc_4 + c_5/\epsilon) + c_6\epsilon^{c_7}\exp(Tc_8) + c_9\epsilon^2$
- $\exp(Tc_4 + c_5/\epsilon)$ - linear in T. No Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 17:** Similar to 12. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 18:** $c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2\exp(c_2/T) + c_3\exp(c_4/T)\log(c_5\epsilon+1) + c_6\exp(c_7\epsilon^{c_8} + c_9/T)$
- $\exp(c/T)$ terms, $\log$ terms. No Gaussian in T. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 19:** $Tc_0 + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + T^{c_3}c_4\epsilon + c_5 + c_6\exp(c_7\epsilon) + c_8\exp(Tc_9\epsilon)$
- If $c_3=1$: $T(c_0+c_4\epsilon) + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + c_5 + c_6\exp(c_7\epsilon) + c_8\exp(Tc_9\epsilon)$
- GT needs $\epsilon T$ and $\epsilon\exp(-\text{quadratic in T})$. This has $\exp(Tc_9\epsilon)$ which is linear in T in exponent, not quadratic. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 20:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1 + c_2\epsilon + c_3\exp(Tc_4 + c_5/\epsilon) + c_6\epsilon^{c_7}\exp(Tc_8)$
- $T^{1/3}$ not $T$. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 21:** $Tc_0 + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + c_3 + c_4\exp(c_5\epsilon) + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon^{c_8}\exp(c_9/T)$
- Not linear in $\epsilon$. $\exp(c/T)$ not Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 22:** $Tc_0\epsilon + c_1 + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon + c_5\exp(Tc_6 + c_7/\epsilon) + c_8\log(Tc_9+1)$
- Has $T\epsilon$ (good!). But $\exp(Tc_6 + c_7/\epsilon)$ is linear in T in exponent. $\log(T)$ term. No Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 23:** $T^{c_0}c_1\log(c_2\epsilon+1) + c_3\epsilon + c_4\log(Tc_5\epsilon^{c_6}+1) + c_7\epsilon^{c_8}$
- $\log$ terms, no Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 24:** Similar to 4. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 25:** $\sqrt{T}c_0\log(c_1\epsilon+1) + Tc_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^{c_3} + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon\exp(c_7/T) + c_8\epsilon^2\exp(Tc_9)$
- $\sqrt{T}$, $\exp(c/T)$, $\exp(cT)$ (linear). No Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 26:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^5 + c_2\log(c_3\epsilon\exp(Tc_4)+1) + c_5\epsilon\exp(Tc_6) + c_7\epsilon^{c_8}\exp(Tc_9)$
- $T^{1/3}$, $\log$, exp linear in T. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 27:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2 + c_2\exp(Tc_3 + c_4/\sqrt{\epsilon}) + Tc_1 + Tc_2\exp(c_3\epsilon) + c_4 + c_5\exp(c_6\epsilon) + c_7\exp(Tc_8 + c_9/\sqrt{\epsilon})$

Wait, re-reading: $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + Tc_1 + Tc_2\exp(c_3\epsilon) + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5 + c_6\exp(c_3\epsilon) + c_7\exp(Tc_8 + c_9/\sqrt{\epsilon})$
- $T^{1/3}$, not linear in $\epsilon$. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 28:** $T^{c_0}c_1\epsilon + c_2 + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5\exp(Tc_6 + c_7/\epsilon) + c_8\log(Tc_9+1)$
- If $c_0=1$: $Tc_1\epsilon + ...$. But $\exp(Tc_6 + c_7/\epsilon)$ is linear in T, $\log$ term. No Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 29:** $T^{1/3}c_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^2 + c_2\exp(Tc_3 + c_4\epsilon^{c_5}) + c_6\sin(Tc_7 + c_8)$
- $T^{1/3}$, $\sin$ term. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 30:** $c_0 + c_1\epsilon + c_2\exp(Tc_3 + c_4/\epsilon) + c_5\log(Tc_6+1) + c_7\epsilon\exp(c_8/T)$
- $\log$, $\exp(c/T)$. No Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 31:** Similar. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 32:** $\sqrt{T}$, $\log$ terms. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 33:** $Tc_0 + Tc_1\exp(c_2\epsilon) + c_3 + c_4\exp(c_5\epsilon) + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon^{c_8}\exp(c_9/T)$
- Not linear in $\epsilon$. $\exp(c/T)$ not Gaussian. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 34-50:** Let me check the remaining ones for the key feature: a term that can produce $\epsilon\exp(-(T-c)^2)$ = $\epsilon\exp(aT^2 + bT + c)$.

**Candidate 35:** $Tc_0\epsilon + c_1\epsilon^{c_2}\exp(Tc_3) + c_4\epsilon + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\log(c_7\epsilon^{c_8}\exp(Tc_9)+1)$
- The $\log$ term and exp linear in T. No quadratic T in exponent. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 36-50:** None of these candidates have $\exp(\text{quadratic in } T)$ or $\exp(-(T-c)^2)$. They all have either $\exp(cT)$ (linear), $\exp(c/T)$, $T^{1/3}$, $\log$, $\sin$, etc.

Let me do a final careful scan for any candidate that could produce a Gaussian in T. The GT requires $\exp(-(T-c)^2) = \exp(-T^2 + 2cT - c^2)$, which needs a $T^2$ term in the exponent.

Looking through all candidates, I see terms like:
- $\exp(Tc + ...)$ - linear in T
- $\exp(c/T)$ - inverse T
- None have $\exp(T^2...)$ or $\exp(-(T-c)^2)$

None of the candidates can produce the Gaussian term in T that the GT requires.
